<span id="freeTextContainer14761912885725668941">Cruising 35,000 feet above the earth, a twin-engine commercial jet encounters an accident that leaves 3 dead, 56 wounded, and the cabin in shambles. What happened? With a multi-billion-dollar company-saving deal on the line, Casey Singleton is sent by her hard-driving boss to uncover the mysterious circumstances that led to the disaster before more people die. But someone</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14761912885725668941">Cruising 35,000 feet above the earth, a twin-engine commercial jet encounters an accident that leaves 3 dead, 56 wounded, and the cabin in shambles. What happened? With a multi-billion-dollar company-saving deal on the line, Casey Singleton is sent by her hard-driving boss to uncover the mysterious circumstances that led to the disaster before more people die. But someone doesn't want her to find the truth. <em>Airframe</em> bristles with authentic information, technical jargon, and the command of detail Crichton's readers have come to expect. Check out Amazon.com's <em>Airframe feature</em> and read an excerpt from the book!</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262915530" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3920693-richard-reviles-censorship-always-in-all-ways" class="left imgcol" title="Richard Reviles Censorship Always in All Ways"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448483618p2/3920693.jpg" alt="Richard Reviles Censorship Always in All Ways" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/262915530?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 14, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3920693-richard-reviles-censorship-always-in-all-ways" class="user" title="Richard Reviles Censorship Always in All Ways">Richard Reviles Censorship Always in All Ways</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer262915530">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7497671488349739432">Rating: 3.5 breathless stars of five<br /><br />I really hate flying. I'm not scared of it, I just dislike being herded into inky-dinky seats meant for short people by ill-tempered sky-waiters who charge for pillows and booze, and then I have to pay more than I used to make a week for the privilege of being searched, patted by men I'm not attracted to in places I don't want to be patted unless I am, etc etc etc.<br /><br />Fifteen years ago, all that was more or less to come, and storymonger Crichton used planes for a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7497671488349739432">Rating: 3.5 breathless stars of five<br /><br />I really hate flying. I'm not scared of it, I just dislike being herded into inky-dinky seats meant for short people by ill-tempered sky-waiters who charge for pillows and booze, and then I have to pay more than I used to make a week for the privilege of being searched, patted by men I'm not attracted to in places I don't want to be patted unless I am, etc etc etc.<br /><br />Fifteen years ago, all that was more or less to come, and storymonger Crichton used planes for a very different kind of tale. What happens to cause a huge section of a plane to go *flooey*, killing a few people and making the entire world nervous about flying? We're about to find out, Casey Singleton and the reader that is. We're going to go into surprisingly interesting amounts of detail about the structure, the manufacture, the sales, the service, the use of airplanes, and how a careful planner could cause huge havoc in a few, small, seemingly innocuous ways.<br /><br />I miss Michael Crichton. He understood the value of detail, the urgency of tight plotting, and the uncomplicated pleasure of following a complicated and logical plot to its only possible ending. If I didn't have Steve Berry, I'd be visiting Crichton's grave once a year with 200 roses to mourn his passing.<br /><br />LitSnobs take note...turn up your noses and all that happens is us groundlings who like books that are fun get an unobstructed view of your boogers.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7497671488349739432">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1419047749">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1419047749" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/22110057-debbie-zapata" class="left imgcol" title="Debbie Zapata"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451631863p2/22110057.jpg" alt="Debbie Zapata" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1419047749?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22110057-debbie-zapata" class="user" title="Debbie Zapata">Debbie Zapata</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1778863.Airframe" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345412997" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/22110057-debbie-zapata?shelf=saturday" class="actionLinkLite">saturday</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1419047749">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer176112075099321057">I read this book aloud to my husband during the past week or so, and parts of it were very dramatic, but other parts (all those charts!) were a bit dull even though we knew they were important. I don't know how a narrator for an audio version would read them, I either handed the book to Marco and let him see for himself, or else I just said 'lots of numbers that I am not going to read'. We got the gist of it all anyway.<br /><br />Casey Singleton is in charge of a team trying to figure out what went wrong o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText176112075099321057">I read this book aloud to my husband during the past week or so, and parts of it were very dramatic, but other parts (all those charts!) were a bit dull even though we knew they were important. I don't know how a narrator for an audio version would read them, I either handed the book to Marco and let him see for himself, or else I just said 'lots of numbers that I am not going to read'. We got the gist of it all anyway.<br /><br />Casey Singleton is in charge of a team trying to figure out what went wrong on flight 545, which did not crash but had a severe inflight 'incident'. There are many layers to what is involved, and it seems that everyone around her has some reason to keep her from finding out the truth. Typical Chrichton fast moving story, but it does tend to porpoise a bit just like the plane itself did. We would just get super interested in the action when the story would stall out into technical details or background or the introduction of a new character and take a nosedive. <br /><br />I learned a great new expression, shouted in disgust by one of the airplane manufacturer's engineers when he is examining the engine and discovers something that is not the way it should be, even though he insists it could not have contributed to the 'incident'. <em>"Fuck a hairy duck!" </em> With apologies to anyone who may be offended by that, I hope I can remember to use it once in awhile! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="176112075099321057">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/291333-jay" class="left imgcol" title="Jay"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1260542911p2/291333.jpg" alt="Jay" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/4807438?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 20, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/291333-jay" class="user" title="Jay">Jay</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4807438">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10626219636871189037">Mike gave me this book when we visited him, Anna, and Kaley at their Woodbridge apt--jesus it must be 3 or 4 (or 5?) years ago. I remember how funny he was about it. Convo went something like this:<br /><br />------------<br /><br />MS: Hey Jay - I got this book for you to have<br /><br />me: Oh really? Well, what's it about?<br /><br />MS: Pfft... fuck if I know. Anna tried it. I tried it. Too many goddamn acronyms in it. <br /><br />me: (laughs)<br /><br />MS: I'm serious, dude. It's all about an airliner crash. But the fuckin author uses every acronym under the s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10626219636871189037">Mike gave me this book when we visited him, Anna, and Kaley at their Woodbridge apt--jesus it must be 3 or 4 (or 5?) years ago. I remember how funny he was about it. Convo went something like this:<br /><br />------------<br /><br />MS: Hey Jay - I got this book for you to have<br /><br />me: Oh really? Well, what's it about?<br /><br />MS: Pfft... fuck if I know. Anna tried it. I tried it. Too many goddamn acronyms in it. <br /><br />me: (laughs)<br /><br />MS: I'm serious, dude. It's all about an airliner crash. But the fuckin author uses every acronym under the sun. NTSB this.. FAA that.. The FBI, the CIA, the PIC, SIC, OR--I'm like Grrrr FUCK THIS BOOK. I tried several times. Can't do it.<br /><br />me: (probably spitting my wine all over the balcony and choking on my laughter)<br /><br />MS: Dude take it. I'm serious. You're a pilot. You can decipher all these fuckin codes. I'm giving it to you or we burn it here and now.<br /><br />me: Okay, Mikey - I'll take it.<br /><br />------------<br /><br />And that's why it sits on my bookshelf today.<br /><br />Was it good? I honestly don't remember every detail, but I enjoyed it. But mostly I enjoy thinking about that night. We were also visiting Mike n Anna at that apt when my dad called and told me my Nanny died. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_44991893">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44991893" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1711431-eric-w" class="left imgcol" title="Eric_W"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1429386336p2/1711431.jpg" alt="Eric_W" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/44991893?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 31, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1711431-eric-w" class="user" title="Eric_W">Eric_W</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1711431-eric-w?shelf=mysteries-and-thrillers" class="actionLinkLite">mysteries-and-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer44991893">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2876971004998957920">This is my first Crichton since the Andromeda Strain written so many years ago. Another reason to ignore the professional critics who have not been terribly kind to Crichton in the past few years. I really liked this book. It has a marvelous blend of science, information and a good plot that keeps the pages turning.<br /><br />It’s interesting that many of the reviews I read focused on the aircraft industry. I think the book is more about the media and it’s relentless pursuit of the visual and the sound bit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2876971004998957920">This is my first Crichton since the Andromeda Strain written so many years ago. Another reason to ignore the professional critics who have not been terribly kind to Crichton in the past few years. I really liked this book. It has a marvelous blend of science, information and a good plot that keeps the pages turning.<br /><br />It’s interesting that many of the reviews I read focused on the aircraft industry. I think the book is more about the media and it’s relentless pursuit of the visual and the sound bite at the expense of truth and the whole picture more than about airplanes.<br /><br />Enroute from Hong Kong to Denver, a brand new Norton-22, a plane clearly modeled on the Boeing 747, pitches and dives like a porpoise before being brought under control. The violent maneuvers kill three passengers and injures 56 others. . The airline's VP in charge of quality assurance — Casey Singleton — has to find out why, before more passengers and the airline's future go into a tailspin. As always in Crichton's expert hands, readers learn a lot about science while becoming enmeshed in the power-plays, office politics, and pressures of the global market and American jobs. Her job is complicated, because, as we gradually learn, powers within the company are trying to manipulate her and to embarrass the company so that the president of the company can be forced out in favor of another. Casey is saddled with a Norton family nephew who turns out to be a spy for one of the other company officers. We learn a great deal about aircraft manufacture and design — I must admit to really loving the technical detail — as Casey tries to figure out why the cockpit reports of turbulence differ from physical evidence of a “commanded slat deployment,” something, that even had it occurred at altitude and high speed should not have caused the plane to go out-of-control the way it appears to have done.<br /><br />Crichton obviously doesn’t like lawyers, their stoolies (an ex-FAA employee who testifies for the plaintiffs in injury suits figures prominently in the media’s desire to create a nasty story) nor the media, and a character clearly modeled after Mike Wallace has few redeeming qualities. At one point Casey is to be interviewed by the Wallace character, Marty Reardon, and a company PR person comes by to help her prepare a little. “There’s only one more thing I can tell you, Katherine. You work in a complex business. If you try to explain that complexity to Marty, you’ll be frustrated. You’ll feel he isn’t interested. He’ll probably cut you off. Because he isn’t interested. A lot of people complain television lacks focus. But that’s the nature of the medium. Television’s not about information at all. Information is active, engaging. Television is passive. Information is disinterested, objective. Television is emotional. It’s entertainment. . . . [Marty’s:] paid to exercise his one reliable talent: provoking people, getting them to make an emotional outburst, to lose their temper, to say something outrageous. He doesn’t really want to know about airplanes. He wants a media moment.”<br /><br />Casey’s father was a journalist and an old friend of his remarks at the end of the book, “Used to be — in the old days-- the media image roughly corresponded to reality. But now it’s all reversed. The media image is the reality, and by comparison day-to-day life seems to lack excitement. So now day-to-day life is false, and the media image is true. Sometimes I look around my living room, and the most real thing in the room is the television. It’s bright and vivid, and the rest of my life looks drab. So I turn the damn thing off. That does it every time. Get my life back.”<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2876971004998957920">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/163018553?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 17, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/652955-linda" class="user" title="Linda">Linda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer163018553">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2413109203769597788">As someone who worked most of my life in Aerospace, on the supersonic B-1 bomber, and then on several Titan missile and launch vehicle programs, I found the book well researched. There were a few times when I said to myself, "In what manufacturing area would THAT occur?" But he's right on with the incessant use of acronyms, and the increasing prevalence of cost-cutting maneuvers that end up compromising flight safety. <br /><br />And I believe he's right on about the maneuvers of the airline companies that</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2413109203769597788">As someone who worked most of my life in Aerospace, on the supersonic B-1 bomber, and then on several Titan missile and launch vehicle programs, I found the book well researched. There were a few times when I said to myself, "In what manufacturing area would THAT occur?" But he's right on with the incessant use of acronyms, and the increasing prevalence of cost-cutting maneuvers that end up compromising flight safety. <br /><br />And I believe he's right on about the maneuvers of the airline companies that buy the airframes and follow (or don't follow) the recommended maintenance procedures. However, never having worked for an airline or been familiar with their maintenance programs, I can't say that with certainty.<br /><br />I liked the female aerospace manager, having been one myself, and while others on Goodreads have written here that Crichton tends to populate his books with stereotypical characters, I say hooray for acknowledging that there are now women in aerospace who (a) have engineering degrees and well-honed critical thinking skills, and (b) have drilled through the difficult-to-penetrate glass ceiling.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2413109203769597788">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9414030056006007879">This was my first Michael Crighton book (I know, I know, I'm an idiot for never reading him before). <br /><br />I really enjoyed Airframe. It was a fast paced techno mystery from the first to the last. I feel like I learned a lot about the design, manufacturing and flying of commercial aircraft. I also learned how lax the quality control is for airlines (seriously, I might never fly again). <br /><br />Casey is a quality investigator for an airplane manufacturer who is sent to investigate an incident that occurred inv</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9414030056006007879">This was my first Michael Crighton book (I know, I know, I'm an idiot for never reading him before). <br /><br />I really enjoyed Airframe. It was a fast paced techno mystery from the first to the last. I feel like I learned a lot about the design, manufacturing and flying of commercial aircraft. I also learned how lax the quality control is for airlines (seriously, I might never fly again). <br /><br />Casey is a quality investigator for an airplane manufacturer who is sent to investigate an incident that occurred involving one of her company's planes. Her job is to determine what actually happened and whether it was human error or a defect in the plane.<br /><br />You might be thinking that this sounds boring but trust me when I say that it is anything but. If you are looking for a good mystery or even just a page turner, don't miss this one.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1257673490">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257673490" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8187431-rade" class="left imgcol" title="Rade "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1426096920p2/8187431.jpg" alt="Rade " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1257673490?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8187431-rade" class="user" title="Rade ">Rade </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8187431-rade?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1257673490">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15969994861644902940">One of those books that I liked but did not like enough. Like most of his other books, this one is well researched by Crichton but I guess not enough to hold my full attention. <br /><br />The beginning was "fun", for a lack of a better word (how fun can airplane accidents be?!?) and even the whole technology mumbo jumbo was somewhat fun (trust me, there is a lot of it) but than the political thing came along where contracts were threatened due to safety issues/concerns and my brain tried to turn itself off</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15969994861644902940">One of those books that I liked but did not like enough. Like most of his other books, this one is well researched by Crichton but I guess not enough to hold my full attention. <br /><br />The beginning was "fun", for a lack of a better word (how fun can airplane accidents be?!?) and even the whole technology mumbo jumbo was somewhat fun (trust me, there is a lot of it) but than the political thing came along where contracts were threatened due to safety issues/concerns and my brain tried to turn itself off. I kept it on but the batteries were losing power up there. I understand at some point it will get all business-y but I wasn't looking forward to it. <br /><br />The ending was good but I feel like it was not big enough hook or a twist to make me give the book enough stars. Still, I am giving it at least 3 stars just because I like Crichton and his style. <br /><br />This one is on a "mehh" scale for me but that is not to say that it was a bad book or a bad read. In fact, I could have read this book in a day or two if I did not have work. Chapters were few pages each and they read very fast. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15969994861644902940">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_78408980">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78408980" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1090620-ed" class="left imgcol" title="Ed"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1208403306p2/1090620.jpg" alt="Ed" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/78408980?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 27, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1090620-ed" class="user" title="Ed">Ed</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Chrichton fans and people with no other choice.</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1090620-ed?shelf=legal-fiction-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">legal-fiction-thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1090620-ed?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer78408980">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17359726703314616747">When <a title="Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton</a> is good he is very, very good but this effort is just plain horrible. The only reason I finished it is due to my obsession about not wanting to miss anything. I found myself reading the first sentence of paragraphs and skipping the rest to move more quickly to the end. I don't think I missed anything doing it that way.<br /><br />The characters are stereotyped beyond belief: the hard working but put upon single mother, the brusque and impatient boss, the techy nerds, the debonair test</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17359726703314616747">When <a title="Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton</a> is good he is very, very good but this effort is just plain horrible. The only reason I finished it is due to my obsession about not wanting to miss anything. I found myself reading the first sentence of paragraphs and skipping the rest to move more quickly to the end. I don't think I missed anything doing it that way.<br /><br />The characters are stereotyped beyond belief: the hard working but put upon single mother, the brusque and impatient boss, the techy nerds, the debonair test pilot, the slimy industrial spy, the good-hearted mentor, the young, overly ambitious news producer, and on and on.<br /><br />The plot involves an incident on a Norton Aircraft passenger liner that is complicated by a pending sale of the same model to China, a union action to stall manufacturing offsets going to China as a condition of the sale, internal company politics, and a pending "Newsline" story about unsafe Norton aircraft. There may have been others. Chrichton had to do something to fill 400+ pages.<br /><br />I had pretty much figured out how it was going to end about 150 pages in. Except for some details, I made a pretty accurate guess. There were a few surprises but overall it was a predictable story with a predictable ending. I wonder if the aircraft industry subsidized Chrichton's efforts.<br /><br />On the positive side, I did learn some things about the aircraft industry, how accidents are investigated, and more than I wanted to know about the acronyms used in the industry.<br /><br />If you are a died in the wool Crichton fan or are stuck on a long flight with nothing else to read, I can recommend this book to you. Other than that there are just too many good Michael Crichton books as well as books about the aircraft industry. You would be better served reading those. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17359726703314616747">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_151240184">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151240184" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2224905-bob-milne" class="left imgcol" title="Bob Milne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452018499p2/2224905.jpg" alt="Bob Milne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/151240184?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 28, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2224905-bob-milne" class="user" title="Bob Milne">Bob Milne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1206780.Airframe" title="ebook 9780375412219" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer151240184">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13472420643264244825">Airframe is - for better or for worse, depending on your point of view - exactly what we've come to expect from a Michael Crichton novel. There's a big-budget action sequence to get us going, a myriad of technological details, a mystery to be solved, a conspiracy driving things in the background, one well-developed protagonist, and a cast of supporting players that really don't exist beyond their role in the plot.<br /><br />Having said all that, it's also a novel I finished over the course of a weekend.<br /><br />The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13472420643264244825">Airframe is - for better or for worse, depending on your point of view - exactly what we've come to expect from a Michael Crichton novel. There's a big-budget action sequence to get us going, a myriad of technological details, a mystery to be solved, a conspiracy driving things in the background, one well-developed protagonist, and a cast of supporting players that really don't exist beyond their role in the plot.<br /><br />Having said all that, it's also a novel I finished over the course of a weekend.<br /><br />The technology is, as always, intriguing without being overwhelming. Crichton doesn't just spew facts at the reader. Instead, you feel as if you're discovering and understanding along with the characters in the story. The mystery is a simple one -- what caused the disaster? -- with more than enough suspense to keep the reader interested. The conspiracy may be a little too obvious for readers of his other works, but it still works.<br /><br />Overall, Airframe is certainly no Jurrasic Park or Disclosure, but it's much better than weaker efforts such as Sphere or Congo. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13472420643264244825">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_837104931">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/837104931" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9972073-dylan-nugent" class="left imgcol" title="Dylan Nugent"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1338753750p2/9972073.jpg" alt="Dylan Nugent" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/837104931?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 28, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9972073-dylan-nugent" class="user" title="Dylan Nugent">Dylan Nugent</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer837104931">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11260582221101177283">Michael Crichton is a master of taking complicated subjects and easing the reader into them while at the same time making the characters seem well immersed in the details. Airframe is a novel about airplanes, and specifically an investigation into a plane accident by the plane's manufacturer. Though all the characters know more about airplanes than you ever will, Crichton has presented a spectacular mixture of in-depth research and understandable explanations. Not only by the end of the novel di</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11260582221101177283">Michael Crichton is a master of taking complicated subjects and easing the reader into them while at the same time making the characters seem well immersed in the details. Airframe is a novel about airplanes, and specifically an investigation into a plane accident by the plane's manufacturer. Though all the characters know more about airplanes than you ever will, Crichton has presented a spectacular mixture of in-depth research and understandable explanations. Not only by the end of the novel did I understand way more about airplanes, including not only the machines themselves but also the complex politics behind the manufacturing industry, but I quickly found myself following along with the technical details of the investigation. This is a mystery novel, filled with suspense and even a couple action scenes, and it kept me engaged throughout. I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11260582221101177283">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

              <a href="/review/list/17209090-richard-jr?shelf=suspense-action" class="actionLinkLite">suspense-action</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer658831491">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3859771073748042763"> Crichton has a true best seller here that holds the attention all the way through the 400+ pages. <br /><br />I like the fact that his protagonist is a gutsy lady who is working with a bunch of engineers in an aircraft plant. She knows how to hold her own and that takes a lot when you know how engineers manage their interpersonal relations and staff. <br /><br />I like the portrayal of the television media for what many of them are; vampires for the latest blood and gore, willing to sacrifice the real explanation of a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3859771073748042763"> Crichton has a true best seller here that holds the attention all the way through the 400+ pages. <br /><br />I like the fact that his protagonist is a gutsy lady who is working with a bunch of engineers in an aircraft plant. She knows how to hold her own and that takes a lot when you know how engineers manage their interpersonal relations and staff. <br /><br />I like the portrayal of the television media for what many of them are; vampires for the latest blood and gore, willing to sacrifice the real explanation of a complex problem for the simple answer which brings off the instantaneous hype in 30 second bytes. <br /><br />The story line is fleshed out with a few side trips to examine our heroine's family life and extra curricular bedtime, but not so much that it detracts from a really great story about how we view airplane disasters, how little we as the general public really know about keeping a million pounds of steel in the air for 12 hours at a time and how blase' we have become about safe comfortable aircraft travel. <br /><br />The behind the scenes plant operations, the union actions and the administrative infighting for power are straight out of the jungle of human relations. I love the way Casey is finally able to turn the tables on the unscrupulous duo of Marder and Richman. We'll miss tha fact that Crichton is no longer with us and able to continue to stimulate our imaginations to such a high degree. <br /><br />I didn't put the book down for the last 200 pages despite the dishes piling up and the dog scratching at the door. Read the first half in bits to absorb the data and then save the last half for when you have a real chance to break away and complete it in one marathon sitting! <br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com/-/e/B001K8HIXI" target="_blank">http://www.amazon.com/-/e/B001K8HIXI</a><a title="Kalahari by Rick McBee" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3881024.Kalahari">

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer378924333">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5174614253203112191">Whenever I want to get back in the swing of reading, I pick an easy read. That’s what this book is – easy. It’s about an airplane crash, the media’s desire to sensationalize instead of report the news, and the politics of the airplane business. It has little character development, and much of the dialogue is driven by explaining how airplanes and the airplane business operate (there is always some dumb character around to ask the obvious question that results in a mini lecture). I suppose if air</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5174614253203112191">Whenever I want to get back in the swing of reading, I pick an easy read. That’s what this book is – easy. It’s about an airplane crash, the media’s desire to sensationalize instead of report the news, and the politics of the airplane business. It has little character development, and much of the dialogue is driven by explaining how airplanes and the airplane business operate (there is always some dumb character around to ask the obvious question that results in a mini lecture). I suppose if airplanes interest you, you might find some aspects to this book interesting. I still found the book intriguing even though I don’t really know much about airplanes, nor do I especially care to. I wasn’t as glued to the story as I was to some other Crichton novels, but it’s still a decent book if that’s the kind of book you like. I give it three stars out of five.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1459869407">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1459869407" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/45942157-lee-lublin" class="left imgcol" title="Lee Lublin"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Lee Lublin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1459869407?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/45942157-lee-lublin" class="user" title="Lee Lublin">Lee Lublin</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1459869407">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10954690092423315436">Airframe was the third Creaton book I read in a row (after park and lost world), and I have to say, it is different, besides instead of being about killer dinosaurs it is about airplanes and how they work. While the park and world were more action based, this story is more like a mystery. And unlike a lot of books and stories, where it is pretty obvious what happened and who did it, it actually stays a mystery for the whole story. While some of the characters are just cookie cutter stereotypes,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10954690092423315436">Airframe was the third Creaton book I read in a row (after park and lost world), and I have to say, it is different, besides instead of being about killer dinosaurs it is about airplanes and how they work. While the park and world were more action based, this story is more like a mystery. And unlike a lot of books and stories, where it is pretty obvious what happened and who did it, it actually stays a mystery for the whole story. While some of the characters are just cookie cutter stereotypes, others characters are very interesting and fun to read about. Luckily, the main character is the latter. There are also a few plot twists that are either hit or miss. Some of them, like what caused the crash, are genius and so unexpected. Other ones, like who is trying to set up the company for failure, are so obvious you know they are bad the second you meet them. Overall, this was a fun and interesting read.<br />	“Sometimes I look around my living room, and the most real thing in the room is the television. It’s bright and vivid, and the rest of my life looks drab. So I turn the damn thing off. That does it every time. Get my life back (Creaton 423).” This quote, while something not that important to the story, is very important in our modern lives. I think this quote also goes along with the essential question, In a culture where we are bombarded with ideas and images of what we should be, how does one form an identity that remains true and authentic to themselves. With all the celebrities on tv and social media showing us how glamorous their lives are and telling you how you should live yours. Weather out of jealousy, attraction, respect, or just plain wanting more out of life, people will try to live their lives like celebrities and abandon what made them them. What this quote teaches us is that if you start to feel like your life is boring, turn the tv off, and go do something about it. Get your life back, and then you can change it if needed. I think this is a quote everyone should take to heart.<br />	I would recommend this book to people who just love a good mystery. While the characters are a little too basic at some point, overall the mystery is well written and you are kept in suspense the whole time. I would also recommend this book to people that love Michael Creaton stories, as this book is just as well written as his other ones. Overall, out of the three Creaton books I have read, this is better then Lost World, but not as good as Jurassic Park.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10954690092423315436">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer514619351">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14794380498984190008">Learnt a few things<br /><br />1. Disasters are often caused by a sequence of unfortunate incidents.<br />2. Record keeping is a good thing.<br />3. Humans ARE the weakest link.<br />4. Don't let your kid fly your plane. <br />5. Wear seatbelts, just in case.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1108252395">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1108252395" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1266077-stephen-gallup" class="left imgcol" title="Stephen Gallup"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1321228329p2/1266077.jpg" alt="Stephen Gallup" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1108252395?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 17, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1266077-stephen-gallup" class="user" title="Stephen Gallup">Stephen Gallup</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7676.Airframe" title="Hardcover 9780963192578" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1108252395">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13331705977124106719">I'm working my way through a couple other books but felt the need for a change of pace this weekend and took a break with <em>Airframe</em>. It was a quick, engaging read.<br /><br />It's one of those stories rooted in detailed understanding of an arcane subject--in this case the intricacies of commercial aircraft design (fleshed out with excursions into rivalry among manufacturers and carrier problems such as the effects of deregulation). I tend to like such stories, especially when those esoteric details actually</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13331705977124106719">I'm working my way through a couple other books but felt the need for a change of pace this weekend and took a break with <em>Airframe</em>. It was a quick, engaging read.<br /><br />It's one of those stories rooted in detailed understanding of an arcane subject--in this case the intricacies of commercial aircraft design (fleshed out with excursions into rivalry among manufacturers and carrier problems such as the effects of deregulation). I tend to like such stories, especially when those esoteric details actually contribute to the plot, which is definitely the case here.<br /><br />And yet at its core this is not about the airplane business nearly as much as it is a statement about the info-tainment business and the people who manipulate news in order to achieve an effect and advance an agenda.<br /><br />The slightly technical background, explained very smoothly for the reader's benefit as the experienced characters bring a newbie up to speed, serves to introduce a company with a good product and competent employees, notwithstanding labor unrest and infighting among top management. <em>And</em> some recent bad luck involving their widebody, the N-22.<br /><br />That bad luck draws the attention of an ambitious junior newscaster named Jennifer, who needs to fill an unplanned gap in her show's weekend programming. But her purpose has nothing to do with educating the viewing public on what has happened. In her world, news needs to be "shaped:"<br /><br /><em>"The best frames engaged the viewer by presenting the story as conflict between good and bad, a morality story. Because the audience got that. If you framed a story that way, you got instant acceptance."</em><br /><br />Jennifer wants to produce a segment in which the makers of the N-22 are introduced to the world as soulless, profit-crazed monsters, a segment that will convince air travelers to shun their planes. Her boss, who already holds default opinions in line with that angle, says, "Perfect! Scare the hell out of everybody."<br /><br />Casey Singleton (interesting name, by the way, as she's introduced as a divorced mom) is in charge of QA at Norton Aircraft. Her job puts her in the hot seat, not merely in the critical project of unraveling the mystery of what happened onboard Flight 545, but in surviving animosity on the shop floor (the union believes management plans to send future assembly work overseas) and more subtle but no less vicious double-dealing among her superiors, and ultimately in standing up the assault Jennifer has launched. All this amounts to a perfect storm for her. Fortunately, when all hell breaks loose she has just handed off her daughter to her ex.<br /><br />The story does follow a sort of formula, and for example Casey's second solo excursion into union domain was a misadventure I saw coming a mile off. But that was not a serious drawback to my enjoyment. I felt completely caught up in the tension leading to the gotcha TV interview, which contains perhaps the best line in the book: "Casey felt like a gladiator being taken into the arena." Casey gets a great line of her own when Jennifer begins to sense that things may not turn out quite as she'd planned:<br /><br />"Listen, maybe we should call this off."<br /><br />"Change the channel?"<br /><br />A plain-spoken old guy, who serves the role of a Greek chorus, offers this insight as an explanation for why punks like Jennifer are allowed to make already-difficult situations so needlessly complicated:<br /><br /><em>"Used to be--in the old days--the media image roughly corresponded to reality. But now it's all reversed. The media image is the reality, and by comparison day-to-day life seems to lack excitement. So now day-to-day life is false, and the media image is true."</em><br /><br />I haven't read everything by Crichton, but that may be the truest observation he has ever put in words.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13331705977124106719">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_927239883">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/927239883" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5675365-simon-howard" class="left imgcol" title="Simon Howard"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1321890913p2/5675365.jpg" alt="Simon Howard" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/927239883?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 03, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5675365-simon-howard" class="user" title="Simon Howard">Simon Howard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer927239883">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3366124538115660339">Before I read this, I’d never read a book by Michael Crichton. As he’s one of the bestselling authors of recent decades, that might come as a surprise. I thought it was time to correct that omission. As someone with an interest in aviation (I’m a fan of trashy TV programmes like Air Crash Investigation, and also the excellent Flaps podcast), I thought Airframe was the perfect option to fill the gap.<br /><br />Airframe is advertised as “a fast-paced, adrenaline-fuelled thriller from the master of high-conce</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3366124538115660339">Before I read this, I’d never read a book by Michael Crichton. As he’s one of the bestselling authors of recent decades, that might come as a surprise. I thought it was time to correct that omission. As someone with an interest in aviation (I’m a fan of trashy TV programmes like Air Crash Investigation, and also the excellent Flaps podcast), I thought Airframe was the perfect option to fill the gap.<br /><br />Airframe is advertised as “a fast-paced, adrenaline-fuelled thriller from the master of high-concept storytelling”. I have some objections to this description: I don’t think it’s fast-paced, adrenaline fuelled, a thriller, or high-concept storytelling. I found it interminably dull.<br /><br />This may be advertised as a thriller, but there were only about three short chase passages during which I could – at even the most generous push of my imaginations – be described as even vaguely interested, let alone thrilled; and those passages played only the most minor of roles in the plot as a whole.<br /><br />The story, such as it was, really described nothing more than a particularly stressful week in the life of a dull woman who works for an aircraft company, combining well-rehearsed plot devices about a woman in a male-dominated work environment with well-rehearsed plot devices describing the conflicted life of a journalist. And it is most certainly not worth sticking with 400 pages of this to reach the damp squib of an ending.<br /><br />Many have criticised Airframe for containing far too much technical detail about the mechanistic of flight; actually, my pre-existing interest in the topic made those sections some of the more interesting bits. But it’s certainly true that pages of technical description does little to heighten the jeopardy of the plot, considering that this is marketed as a thriller.<br /><br />All of which is not to say that the book is bad, per sé: It’s just exceptionally bland. Much like magnolia paint, it’s dull but inoffensive, nobody’s favourite, but disliked very few.<br /><br />I am afraid I am one of the few. I like books which have some sort of impact. This has none. If you like your books bland, you’ll probably get on very well with Airframe, but probably not with me. I struggled to finish it, and cannot recommend it.<br /><br />This review was originally posted at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://sjhoward.co.uk/archive/2013/02/13/review-airframe-by-michael-crichton" target="_blank">http://sjhoward.co.uk/archive/2013/02...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3366124538115660339">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1094900924606688727">DO NOT READ THIS IF YOU PLAN TO TAKE A FLIGHT ANYTIME SOON!<br /><br />I bought this book without even thinking as I waited for my plane from L.A. to Baltimore, Maryland to come in. Two chapters in and I had to put it down because what it talks about is so real you just have to ignore it for the time being. Crichton always does a ton of research for his books, making them feel and appear as if they already happened and you just happen to be getting a behind-the-scenes look into the event and lives of the pe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1094900924606688727">DO NOT READ THIS IF YOU PLAN TO TAKE A FLIGHT ANYTIME SOON!<br /><br />I bought this book without even thinking as I waited for my plane from L.A. to Baltimore, Maryland to come in. Two chapters in and I had to put it down because what it talks about is so real you just have to ignore it for the time being. Crichton always does a ton of research for his books, making them feel and appear as if they already happened and you just happen to be getting a behind-the-scenes look into the event and lives of the people experiening it. <br /><br />Airframe basically takes everything you thought (and especially didn't think of) about the airline industry and lays it out black and white: it is a business, one which is controlled by people who want to make money, especially quick, easy money. How do they do that? By buying cheaper parts from other countries, by cutting staff and cutting the amount of time that staff has to work on a plane, by having less inspections of the aircraft for safety; this book could make some people never want to fly again.<br /><br />Still, a fun read, but if you're already scared of flying, you might just want to stay ignorant.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_62837004">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62837004" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2506057-sarai" class="left imgcol" title="Sarai"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1295027741p2/2506057.jpg" alt="Sarai" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62837004?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 09, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2506057-sarai" class="user" title="Sarai">Sarai</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2506057-sarai?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62837004">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12131884150337837528">From Publishers Weekly<br />...The event that launches the story, conceived long before TWA Flight 800's last takeoff, is an airline disaster. Why did a passenger plane "porpoise"-pitch and dive repeatedly-enroute from Hong Kong to Denver, killing four and injuring 56? That's what Casey Singleton, v-p for quality assurance for Norton Aircraft, has to find out fast. If Norton's design is to blame, its imminent deal with China may collapse, and the huge company along with it. With Casey as his unsubtle</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12131884150337837528">From Publishers Weekly<br />...The event that launches the story, conceived long before TWA Flight 800's last takeoff, is an airline disaster. Why did a passenger plane "porpoise"-pitch and dive repeatedly-enroute from Hong Kong to Denver, killing four and injuring 56? That's what Casey Singleton, v-p for quality assurance for Norton Aircraft, has to find out fast. If Norton's design is to blame, its imminent deal with China may collapse, and the huge company along with it. With Casey as his unsubtle focus-she's one of the few Crichton heroines, an all-American gal who's more plot device than character-Crichton works readers through a brisk course in airline mechanics and safety. The accretion of technical detail, though fascinating, makes for initially slow reading that speeds up only fitfully when Casey is menaced by what seem to be union men angry over the Chinese deal. But as she uncovers numerous anomalies about the accident, and as high corporate intrigue and a ratings-hungry TV news team enter the picture, the plot complicates and suspense rises, peaking high above the earth in an exciting re-creation of the flight. It's possible that Crichton has invented a new subgenre here-the industrial thriller-despite elements (video-generated clues, for one) recycled from his earlier work. It's certain that, while this is no Jurassic Park, he's concocted another slick, bestselling, cinema-ready entertainment.<br /><br />I liked the book better than the above reviewer. I was a bit afraid to read it because I have always feared flying and I thought this might turn me off it forever, but it's more about how well planes are built and how safe they are than what is wrong with planes. It was actually kind of reassuring from that point of view.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12131884150337837528">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_222450964">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222450964" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5786351-brian" class="left imgcol" title="Brian"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1310489385p2/5786351.jpg" alt="Brian" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/222450964?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 12, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5786351-brian" class="user" title="Brian">Brian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer222450964">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18357859762489613523">I've never read Michael Crichton before and after Airframe I'm pretty sure I never will read Crighton again. The plot itself which concerns an inflight accident on an airliner isn't bad. It's the multitude of acronyms (With no glossary for them) and the characters who are essentially caricatures.<br /><br />The story is told mainly through the eyes of Casey Singleton who along with a secretary and a media coach, who is in the book for about four pages, are the only "normal" people in the book. Casey is a VP</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18357859762489613523">I've never read Michael Crichton before and after Airframe I'm pretty sure I never will read Crighton again. The plot itself which concerns an inflight accident on an airliner isn't bad. It's the multitude of acronyms (With no glossary for them) and the characters who are essentially caricatures.<br /><br />The story is told mainly through the eyes of Casey Singleton who along with a secretary and a media coach, who is in the book for about four pages, are the only "normal" people in the book. Casey is a VP/troubleshooter/amateur aviation detective/ for Norton which is the company that built the plane that the book is about. Throughout the book Ms. Singleton deals with a group of characters that is simply not to be believed--Coworkers who are almost all geeks, media personalities who are mainly dishonest, union members who are all dishonest and violent. It just too much. Sweet little Casey and her secretary are the only people who come off as being genuine which makes for a pretty stupid story.<br /><br />The grande finale of the book is simply ridiculous. I won't give anything away and spoil it for other readers. Suffice it to say that what happened never would have been allowed to happen. It's just a joke. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18357859762489613523">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_351751835">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351751835" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5198301-todd-russell" class="left imgcol" title="Todd Russell"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1375999368p2/5198301.jpg" alt="Todd Russell" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/351751835?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 21, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5198301-todd-russell" class="user" title="Todd Russell">Todd Russell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5198301-todd-russell?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5198301-todd-russell?shelf=technology" class="actionLinkLite">technology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer351751835">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3887613884763088484">A fun, engrossing techno thriller that probably shouldn't be read aboard an airplane. Follow along with the VP of Quality Assurance Casey Singleton of a fictional (but seemingly all too real) airframe manufacturer. Casey is assigned to investigate an incident with Flight 545 from Hong Kong that left over fifty people injured and three dead, including a crew member. Casey is one of Crichton's more rounded female characters and considering he isn't known for strong characterization, she is an exce</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3887613884763088484">A fun, engrossing techno thriller that probably shouldn't be read aboard an airplane. Follow along with the VP of Quality Assurance Casey Singleton of a fictional (but seemingly all too real) airframe manufacturer. Casey is assigned to investigate an incident with Flight 545 from Hong Kong that left over fifty people injured and three dead, including a crew member. Casey is one of Crichton's more rounded female characters and considering he isn't known for strong characterization, she is an excellent match for this engaging tale that takes us deep inside just how serious and competitive the airplane manufacturing business can be. Crichton also interweaves a compelling subplot involving a young, aggressive TV news journalist looking to expose what she believes to be a cover up by Casey's company. The ending is solid and wraps up the tale nicely. There are a few suspenseful moments in airplane hangars and plenty of things to be learned in this thriller. Man, I miss Crichton. Recommended.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3887613884763088484">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_42145305">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42145305" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/541343-kenny" class="left imgcol" title="Kenny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446678573p2/541343.jpg" alt="Kenny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/42145305?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 06, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/541343-kenny" class="user" title="Kenny">Kenny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7667.Airframe" title="Paperback 9780099556312" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/541343-kenny?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer42145305">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13238474637672391542">Michael Crichton, literary uber-mensch, sets himself pretty high standards, so one cannot be too disappointed when he fails to outscore JURASSIC PARK every time. But what makes Crichton's books interesting (to me) is not so much the story, but the theme, which is almost always a cautionary tale (JURASSIC PARK: don't mess with mother nature; STATE OF FEAR: you can't mess with mother nature, etc.) AIRFRAME is not about the dangers of air travel, however, as one might suspect from the set-up. Rathe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13238474637672391542">Michael Crichton, literary uber-mensch, sets himself pretty high standards, so one cannot be too disappointed when he fails to outscore JURASSIC PARK every time. But what makes Crichton's books interesting (to me) is not so much the story, but the theme, which is almost always a cautionary tale (JURASSIC PARK: don't mess with mother nature; STATE OF FEAR: you can't mess with mother nature, etc.) AIRFRAME is not about the dangers of air travel, however, as one might suspect from the set-up. Rather, it's about how the media, in a frenzy to get our attention (and often nothing more than that) are willing, capable, and eager to destroy valuable billion-dollar companies, their executives' lives, and the livelihood of the employees, suppliers, and subcontractors -- all because a 14-minute story is needed for a "news" show on Saturday night. I finished the book feeling outraged, and so it was a success (I'm sure that was Crichton's intent), even though the ending was less than satisfying and also somewhat telegraphed. Still, if you want a doctor's stethoscope placed up against the heart of modern trends, no one does (or did it, alas!) better than Dr. Crichton. RIP.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13238474637672391542">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_20828183">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a href="/review/show/20828183?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 23, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/948503-nita-elder" class="user" title="Nita Elder">Nita Elder</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer20828183">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1563090914606011451">Crichton takes the reader into the manufactory of airlines. The story begins with an "incident" over the Pacific, which injures many passengers and kills a few. The story has some loose ends, but Crichton manages to get across his fear that the US is not protecting its international technological position. There are several stories taking place simultaneously. Our protagonist - a divorcee, finally uncovers some pretty disturbing facts which jeapordize the welfare of her company, while she helps</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1563090914606011451">Crichton takes the reader into the manufactory of airlines. The story begins with an "incident" over the Pacific, which injures many passengers and kills a few. The story has some loose ends, but Crichton manages to get across his fear that the US is not protecting its international technological position. There are several stories taking place simultaneously. Our protagonist - a divorcee, finally uncovers some pretty disturbing facts which jeapordize the welfare of her company, while she helps solve what caused the "incident" over the Pacific. Underlying theme - the US should wake up and protect its intellectual property, or we'll fall farther in debt to the European Union and the nations of the Pacific Rim. It's a pretty quick read. The information about airplanes and what makes them work is interesting.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer479563368">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1741780666724304360">Enroute from Asia to Denver, a commercial jet liner experiences an accident at 35,000 feet. The result is three dead, fifty six injured, and the cabin wrecked. Casey Singleton is sent to uncover the cause of this incident. The stakes are high with a multi-billion dollar sale to the Chinese one the line. Someone does not want her to find the truth, however. Is it the tough labor unions who see jobs being exported to China if the deal goes through? Is it someone else? What will they do to stop her</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1741780666724304360">Enroute from Asia to Denver, a commercial jet liner experiences an accident at 35,000 feet. The result is three dead, fifty six injured, and the cabin wrecked. Casey Singleton is sent to uncover the cause of this incident. The stakes are high with a multi-billion dollar sale to the Chinese one the line. Someone does not want her to find the truth, however. Is it the tough labor unions who see jobs being exported to China if the deal goes through? Is it someone else? What will they do to stop her?<br /><br />This was a good fast-paced book with technical acronyms and jargon. While I enjoyed the technical aspects of the investigation, Chrichton introduces much more as is customary with his other works. In this case, it is about power and what some will do to get it or do when they have it. <br /></span>

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer86149690">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17330149298340121905">I read this mainly because I find airplanes and accident forensics fascinating. It's a typical Crichton set up, without and sci fi this time. The solution to the central mystery--what happened on flight 545--is fairly obvious early on so the rest of the book is mainly the suspense of how it will all play out. <br /><br />**Warning-major spoilers ahead**<br />It occurred to me after I finished, however, that the "big twist" part of the plot depended entirely on the two N-22 related accidents taking place one week</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17330149298340121905">I read this mainly because I find airplanes and accident forensics fascinating. It's a typical Crichton set up, without and sci fi this time. The solution to the central mystery--what happened on flight 545--is fairly obvious early on so the rest of the book is mainly the suspense of how it will all play out. <br /><br />**Warning-major spoilers ahead**<br />It occurred to me after I finished, however, that the "big twist" part of the plot depended entirely on the two N-22 related accidents taking place one week before the Big Sale to China, which the bad guys could never have predicted, making that whole part of the story completely ludicrous. It's very possible I missed something there so please feel free to point it out if I did! </span>
